Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. Because this overall table combines data from multiple academic years and because both places and methods have changed over the years, there is some inaccuracy in representing some places. For example, Unthank Hall did not exist before Spring 2022 data collection and Lokey Science Complex was disaggregated in map regions after Spring 2018. So, Unthankâ€™s metrics are likely underestimated, and Lokey Science Complex appears as both an aggregated place and a subordinate place (Spring 2018) with legitimate subordinate places that make up Lokey Science Complex (Spring 2019, Spring 2020, Spring 2022). Spring 2022: Mostly first-year, second-year, third-year, fourth-year, and fifth-year (i.e., 2021-22, 2020-21, 2019-20, 2018-19, and, 2017-18 cohorts, respectively) US undergraduates contributed data, along with a few n-year (i.e., a few from 2002-02, 2007-08, 2010-11, 2011-12, 2014-15, and 2016-17 cohorts) and US exchange undergraduates. East Lawn was mislabeled as West Lawn. So, there is no distinction between East and West Lawns. Spring 2020: First-year, second-year, third-year, fourth-year, and fifth-year (i.e., 2019-20, 2018-19, 2017-18, 2016-17, and 2015-16 cohorts, respectively) US undergraduates contributed data. Spring 2019: First-year, second-year, third-year, and fourth-year (i.e., 2018-19, 2017-18, 2016-17, and 2015-16 cohorts, respectively) US undergraduates contributed data. Baker was mislabeled as Barnhart. So, there is no distinction between Baker and Barnhart. And no region was drawn for Autzen Stadium. Therefore, no click data exist for Autzen. Spring 2018: First-year, second-year, and third-year (i.e., 2017-18, 2016-17, and 2015-16 cohorts, respectively) US undergraduates contributed data. Total nClickBelong = 8,483; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 6,186. Total nStudentBelong = 2,586; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 2,080. Again because this overall table combines data from multiple academic years, some students contributed data more than once. Most students contributed to only one wave of data collection (n = 2,711, 86.4%), some students contributed to two waves (n = 295, 9.4%), and relatively few students contributed to three waves (n = 131, 4.2%). See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. â€œAll Yearsâ€ = Mostly first-year, second-year, third-year, fourth-year, and fifth-year (i.e., 2021-22, 2020-21, 2019-20, 2018-19, and, 2017-18 cohorts, respectively) US undergraduates contributed data, along with a few n-year (i.e., a few from 2002-02, 2007-08, 2010-11, 2011-12, 2014-15, and 2016-17 cohorts) and US exchange undergraduates. East Lawn was mislabeled as West Lawn. Total nClickBelong = 2,601; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 1,954. Total nStudentBelong = 949; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 753. See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. â€œ4th-Yearâ€ = 2018-19 cohort, who were at the end of their fourth year at the UO in Spring 2022, meaning that only fourth-year US undergraduates contributed data. East Lawn was mislabeled as West Lawn. Total nClickBelong = 402; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 301. Total nStudentBelong = 142; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 110. See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. â€œ3rd-Yearâ€ = 2019-20 cohort, who were at the end of their third year at the UO in Spring 2022, meaning that only third-year US undergraduates contributed data. East Lawn was mislabeled as West Lawn. Total nClickBelong = 596; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 461. Total nStudentBelong = 211; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 175. See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. â€œ2nd-Yearâ€ = 2020-21 cohort, who were at the end of their second year at the UO in Spring 2022, meaning that only second-year US undergraduates contributed data. East Lawn was mislabeled as West Lawn. Total nClickBelong = 522; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 434. Total nStudentBelong = 196; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 168. See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. â€œ1st-Yearâ€ = 2021-22 cohort, who were at the end of their first year at the UO in Spring 2022, meaning that only first-year US undergraduates contributed data. East Lawn was mislabeled as West Lawn. Total nClickBelong = 1,009; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 693. Total nStudentBelong = 372; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 275. See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. â€œ1st-through-5th-Yearâ€ = 2019-20, 2018-19, 2017-18, 2016-17, and 2015-16 cohorts (i.e., students who were at the end of their first, second, third, fourth, or fifth years at the UO in Spring 2018, respectively), meaning first-year, second-year, third-year, fourth-year, or fifth-year US undergraduates contributed data. Total nClickBelong = 2,866; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 1,758. Total nStudentBelong = 995; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 709. See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. â€œ4th-Yearâ€ = 2016-17 cohort, who were at the end of their fourth year at the UO in Spring 2020, meaning that only fourth-year US undergraduates contributed data. Total nClickBelong = 338; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 259. Total nStudentBelong = 116; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 95. See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. â€œ3rd-Yearâ€ = 2017-18 cohort, who were at the end of their third year at the UO in Spring 2020, meaning that only third-year US undergraduates contributed data. Total nClickBelong = 300; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 175. Total nStudentBelong = 104; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 72. See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. â€œ2nd-Yearâ€ = 2018-19 cohort, who were at the end of their second year at the UO in Spring 2020, meaning that only second-year US undergraduates contributed data. Total nClickBelong = 805; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 574. Total nStudentBelong = 284; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 229. See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. â€œ1st-Yearâ€ = 2019-20 cohort, who were at the end of their first year at the UO in Spring 2020, meaning that only first-year US undergraduates contributed data. Total nClickBelong = 1,400; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 727. Total nStudentBelong = 483; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 304. See Supplemental Method for more details. Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. â€œ1st-through-4th-Yearâ€ = 2018-19, 2017-18, 2016-17, and 2015-16 cohorts (i.e., students who were at the end of their first, second, third, or fourth years at the UO in Spring 2018, respectively), meaning first-year, second-year, third-year, and fourth-year US undergraduates contributed data. Baker was mislabeled as Barnhart. So, there is no distinction between Baker and Barnhart. And no region was drawn for Autzen Stadium. Therefore, no click data exist for Autzen. Total nClickBelong = 1,814; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 1,439. Total nStudentBelong = 631; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 560. See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. â€œ4th-Yearâ€ = 2015-16 cohort, who were at the end of their fourth year at the UO in Spring 2019, meaning that only fourth-year US undergraduates contributed data. Baker was mislabeled as Barnhart. So, there is no distinction between Baker and Barnhart. And no region was drawn for Autzen Stadium. Therefore, no click data exist for Autzen. Total nClickBelong = 237; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 207. Total nStudentBelong = 81; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 76. See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. â€œ3rd-Yearâ€ = 2016-17 cohort, who were at the end of their third year at the UO in Spring 2019, meaning that only third-year US undergraduates contributed data. Baker was mislabeled as Barnhart. So, there is no distinction between Baker and Barnhart. And no region was drawn for Autzen Stadium. Therefore, no click data exist for Autzen. Total nClickBelong = 396; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 324. Total nStudentBelong = 140; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 126. See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. â€œ2nd-Yearâ€ = 2017-18 cohort, who were at the end of their second year at the UO in Spring 2019, meaning that only second-year US undergraduates contributed data. Baker was mislabeled as Barnhart. So, there is no distinction between Baker and Barnhart. And no region was drawn for Autzen Stadium. Therefore, no click data exist for Autzen. Total nClickBelong = 307; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 253. Total nStudentBelong = 107; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 97. See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. â€œ1st-Yearâ€ = 2018-19 cohort, who were at the end of their first year at the UO in Spring 2019, meaning that only first-year US undergraduates contributed data. Baker was mislabeled as Barnhart. So, there is no distinction between Baker and Barnhart. And no region was drawn for Autzen Stadium. Therefore, no click data exist for Autzen. Total nClickBelong = 874; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 655. Total nStudentBelong = 303; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 261. See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. First-year, second-year, and third-year (i.e., 2017-18, 2016-17, and 2015-16 cohorts, respectively) US undergraduates contributed data. Total nClickBelong = 1,202; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 1,035. Total nStudentBelong = 432; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 399. See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. Because this overall table combines data from multiple academic years, there is some inaccuracy in representing some places. However, because data are limited to Spring 2020 and Spring 2022 and methods were consistent between those waves, apart from a minor mislabeling of lawn regions, inaccuracy in representing places is due to physical changes in places, with the main changes being Unthank and Knight Campus construction. Spring 2022: Degree-seeking (first-year and second-year) and exchange international undergraduates and degree-seeking international graduates contributed data. East Lawn was mislabeled as West Lawn. So, there is no distinction between East and West Lawns. Spring 2020: Freshman, Sophomore, Junior and Senior degree-seeking international undergraduates contributed data. Total nClickBelong = 383; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 223. Total nStudentBelong = 138; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 91. No one contributed data to more than one wave. See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. Freshman, Sophomore, Junior and Senior degree-seeking international undergraduates contributed data. Total nClickBelong = 257; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 167. Total nStudentBelong = 90; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 67. See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

## attr(,"class")
## [1] "reactable"  "htmlwidget"
## attr(,"package")
## [1] "reactable"

Note: All columns are sortable. The default sorting is alphabetical order of Aggregated Place then Place. The Aggregated Place column is searchable. Scroll right to see more metrics on the right side of the table. Use the â€œShowâ€ dropdown to elongate the table up to 100 rows. Click â€œPrevious,â€ â€œNext,â€ or numbers between to move through pages. The table is hierarchically organized: Place within Aggregated Place. Click the triangle next to an Aggregated Place to drop down its list of subordinate Places. Parentheses to the right of Aggregated Place names denote how many subordinate places there are (1 = Aggregated Place and Place are identical). An aggregated place combines places in the Place column that are spatial (e.g., Lokey Science Complex) or conceptual (e.g., University Housing) clusters of many places. Most aggregation is based on campus maps, but the Erb Memorial Union has its own maps and data collection. Consequently, the â€œErb Memorial Unionâ€ entry in the Aggregated Place column contains campus-level data and the â€œEMU-Specific Placesâ€ entry contains EMU-level data. Inclusive is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong are raw counts of how many clicks a place accrued on the â€œbelongâ€ map or â€œdonâ€™t belongâ€ map, respectively. Click Belong and Click Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which a place is considered somewhere students feel like they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively, relative to other places. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total number of Belong or Donâ€™t Belong clicks, respectively, and multiplied by 100. Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are percentages indicating the extent to which students agree that a place is somewhere they feel they belong or donâ€™t belong, respectively. They are computed by dividing n Belong and n Donâ€™t Belong by the total numbers of students who contributed data to those ns, respectively. In other words, inclusive, n Belong, n Donâ€™t Belong, Click Belong, and Click Donâ€™t Belong are all place-based metrics, whereas Student Belong and Student Donâ€™t Belong are person-based metrics. US and international graduates contributed data. East Lawn was mislabeled as West Lawn. So, there is no distinction between East and West Lawns. Total nClickBelong = 305; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 193. Total nStudentBelong = 129; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 82. See Supplemental Method for more details. Table was generated using the reactable package.

Unfortunately, no region for Autzen was drawn on maps in Spring 2019 data collection. So, no click data for that place were recorded. Its quantification is thus denoted with a big red question mark. Total nClick = 307. Total nStudent = 107. See Supplemental Method for more details. Heat map was produced in Qualtrics (30px radius, 35px blur). 5.3.1.3 Spring 2019

5.3.1.3.1 1st-through-4th-Year
5.3.1.3.1.1 Belong
## <pointer: 0x0>
## attr(,"class")
## [1] "magick-image"

Note: ROYGBIV spectrum represents a continuum from more to fewer clicks on a place, given total number of clicks. Number of clicks on a place \(\ge\) 20 are displayed. Color saturation and area of blobs are dependent on concentration in a general area irrespective of regions drawn on a map, which can sometimes be inconsistent with quantification based on clicks in map regions. Additionally, the Erb Memorial Union map in Spring 2019 consisted of two vertically stacked images in presentation during data collection. This produces blob distortion across images, and it results in invalid data; although students were instructed to select up to 3 places, n = 17 selected more than 3. For quantification of maps and other analyses, the first three recorded responses from these few students were used and the rest were discarded. â€œ1st-through-4th-Yearâ€ = 2018-19, 2017-18, 2016-17, and 2015-16 cohorts (i.e., students who were at the end of their first, second, third, or fourth years at the UO in Spring 2018, respectively), meaning first-year, second-year, third-year, and fourth-year US undergraduates contributed data. Total nClick = 916. Total nStudent = 333. See Supplemental Method for more details. Heat map was produced in Qualtrics (30px radius, 35px blur). Click counts were overlaid on the heat map image using the magick package.

5.4 Campus Inclusiveness

5.4.1 Disaggregated and Less Delimited

5.4.1.1 US Undergraduate

5.4.1.1.1 Overall

Note: Rectangle size represents a placeâ€™s overall popularity, computed by n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong. Rectangle color represents a placeâ€™s inclusiveness, which is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. Yellow represents the high end of the inclusiveness continuum and black represents the low end. Gray text represents inclusiveness \(\gt\) 75%. â€œDisaggregatedâ€ = nothing was done to combine individual places into larger places (e.g., residence halls into University Housing). â€œLess Delimitedâ€ = the criterion for inclusion in of a place in a treemap was total click count of at least 20, which is less delimited than the criterion used in â€œMore Delimited.â€ The criterion for presenting a treemap was at least 4 places represented. Additionally, all treemaps omit clicks on Lawn, Other, and Out of Bounds regions. Some names of places with lower popularity were abbreviated to fit the text in their respective rectangles: TF = Turf Field, DS = Duck Store, Barn = Outdoor Program Barn, Cas = Cascade, FAS = Fine Art Studios, MNL = Many Nations Longhouse, MS = LERC Military Science, MNCH = Museum of Natural and Cultural History, Moss = Moss Street Childrenâ€™s Center, Fent = Fenton, LLC = Living Learning Center, Essl = Esslinger, BCC = Black Cultural Center, Mac = McArthur Court, Saun Stad = Saunders Stadium, Friend = Friendly, TI = Tennis Indoor, span style = â€œcolor: #49C1ADâ€>PLC = Prince Lucien Campbell. Because this overall treemap combines data from multiple academic years and because both places and methods have changed over the years, there is some inaccuracy in representing popularity and inclusiveness (treemaps within academic years are accurate, and because there are fewer available data, overall treemap for international students is accurate in this respect despite combining data). For example, Unthank Hall did not exist before Spring 2022 data collection and Lokey Science Complex was disaggregated in map regions after Spring 2018. So, Unthankâ€™s popularity is likely underestimated and its inclusiveness may be, too, and Lokey Science Complex (Spring 2018) is depicted on the treemap along with places that make up Lokey Science Complex (Spring 2019, Spring 2020, Spring 2022). Spring 2022: Mostly first-year, second-year, third-year, fourth-year, and fifth-year (i.e., 2021-22, 2020-21, 2019-20, 2018-19, and, 2017-18 cohorts, respectively) US undergraduates contributed data, along with a few n-year (i.e., a few from 2002-02, 2007-08, 2010-11, 2011-12, 2014-15, and 2016-17 cohorts) and US exchange undergraduates. East Lawn was mislabeled as West Lawn. So, there is no distinction between East and West Lawns. Spring 2020: First-year, second-year, third-year, fourth-year, and fifth-year (i.e., 2019-20, 2018-19, 2017-18, 2016-17, and 2015-16 cohorts, respectively) US undergraduates contributed data. Spring 2019: First-year, second-year, third-year, and fourth-year (i.e., 2018-19, 2017-18, 2016-17, and 2015-16 cohorts, respectively) US undergraduates contributed data. Baker was mislabeled as Barnhart. So, there is no distinction between Baker and Barnhart. And no region was drawn for Autzen Stadium. Therefore, no click data exist for Autzen. Spring 2018: First-year, second-year, and third-year (i.e., 2017-18, 2016-17, and 2015-16 cohorts, respectively) US undergraduates contributed data. Total nClickBelong = 8,483; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 6,186. Total nStudentBelong = 2,586; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 2,080. Again because this overall treemap combines data from multiple academic years, some students contributed data more than once. Most students contributed to only one wave of data collection (2,711, 86.4%), some students contributed to two waves (295, 9.4%), and relatively few students contributed to three waves (131, 4.2%). See Supplemental Method for more details. Treemap was generated using the ggplot2 and treemapify packages. Colors were produced using the inferno palette of the viridis package.

5.4.2 Aggregated and More Delimited

5.4.2.1 US Undergraduate

5.4.2.1.1 Overall

Inclusiveness is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. Yellow represents the high end of the inclusiveness continuum and black represents the low end. Color mapping to inclusiveness percentages comports with the treemaps in the â€œDisaggregated and Less Delimitedâ€ section, and is thus variable across plots. â€œAggregatedâ€ = some individual places were combined into larger places (e.g., residence halls into University Housing). â€œMore Delimitedâ€ = the criterion for inclusion of a place in a plot was \(\geq\) 0.1 of the total proportion of clicks, where total proportion of clicks was defined as the total number of clicks on a place divided by the average of the total number of clicks across all places, which is more delimited than the criterion used in â€œLess Delimited.â€ Clicks on Lawn, Other, and Out of Bounds regions were omitted prior to computing total proportion of clicks. Spring 2022: Mostly first-year, second-year, third-year, fourth-year, and fifth-year (i.e., 2021-22, 2020-21, 2019-20, 2018-19, and, 2017-18 cohorts, respectively) US undergraduates contributed data, along with a few n-year (i.e., a few from 2002-02, 2007-08, 2010-11, 2011-12, 2014-15, and 2016-17 cohorts) and US exchange undergraduates. Spring 2020: First-year, second-year, third-year, fourth-year, and fifth-year (i.e., 2019-20, 2018-19, 2017-18, 2016-17, and 2015-16 cohorts, respectively) US undergraduates contributed data. Spring 2019: First-year, second-year, third-year, and fourth-year (i.e., 2018-19, 2017-18, 2016-17, and 2015-16 cohorts, respectively) US undergraduates contributed data. Spring 2018: First-year, second-year, and third-year (i.e., 2017-18, 2016-17, and 2015-16 cohorts, respectively) US undergraduates contributed data. Total nClickBelong = 8,483; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 6,186. Total nStudentBelong = 2,586; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 2,080. See Supplemental Method for more details. Because this overall bar plot combines data from multiple academic years, some students contributed data more than once. Most students contributed to only one wave of data collection (2,711, 86.4%), some students contributed to two waves (295, 9.4%), and relatively few students contributed to three waves (131, 4.2%). Bar plot was generated using the ggplot2 package. Colors were produced using the inferno palette of the viridis package.

Color mapping to inclusiveness percentages comports with the treemaps in the â€œDisaggregated and Less Delimitedâ€ section, and is thus variable across plots. â€œAggregatedâ€ = some individual places were combined into larger places (e.g., residence halls into University Housing). â€œMore Delimitedâ€ = the criterion for inclusion of a place in a plot was \(\geq\) 0.1 of the total proportion of clicks, where total proportion of clicks was defined as the total number of clicks on a place divided by the average of the total number of clicks across all places, which is more delimited than the criterion used in â€œLess Delimited.â€ Clicks on Lawn, Other, and Out of Bounds regions were omitted prior to computing total proportion of clicks. â€œ1st-Yearâ€ = 2021-22 cohort, who were at the end of their first year at the UO in Spring 2022, meaning that only first-year US undergraduates contributed data. 5.5 Erb Memorial Union Inclusiveness

5.5.1 US Undergraduate

5.5.1.1 Overall

Note: Rectangle size represents a placeâ€™s overall popularity, computed by n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong. Rectangle color represents a placeâ€™s inclusiveness, which is a percentage indicating how inclusive a place is and is computed by n Belong / (n Belong + n Donâ€™t Belong) * 100. Yellow represents the high end of the inclusiveness continuum and black represents the low end. Gray text represents inclusiveness \(\gt\) 75%. The criterion for inclusion of a place in the treemap was total click count of at least 20. The criterion for presentation of a treemap was at least 4 places represented. Additionally, all treemaps omit clicks on Other and Out of Bounds regions. SSC = Student Sustainability Center, Hallway 1 = the East wing hallway on level 1 that runs in front of the Multicultural Center, Hallway 2 = the East wing hallway on level 2 that runs in front of the the Center for Student Involvement Resource Center and the Redwood Auditorium. Because this overall treemap combines data from multiple academic years and because both places and methods have changed over the years, there is some inaccuracy in representing popularity and inclusiveness (treemaps within academic years are accurate). Spring 2022: Mostly first-year, second-year, third-year, fourth-year, and fifth-year (i.e., 2021-22, 2020-21, 2019-20, 2018-19, and, 2017-18 cohorts, respectively) US undergraduates contributed data, along with a few n-year (i.e., a few from 2002-02, 2007-08, 2010-11, 2011-12, 2014-15, and 2016-17 cohorts) and US exchange undergraduates. Spring 2020: First-year, second-year, third-year, fourth-year, and fifth-year (i.e., 2019-20, 2018-19, 2017-18, 2016-17, and 2015-16 cohorts, respectively) US undergraduates contributed data. Spring 2019: First-year, second-year, third-year, and fourth-year (i.e., 2018-19, 2017-18, 2016-17, and 2015-16 cohorts, respectively) US undergraduates contributed data. Spring 2018: First-year, second-year, and third-year (i.e., 2017-18, 2016-17, and 2015-16 cohorts, respectively) US undergraduates contributed data. Total nClickBelong = 4,016; total nClickDonâ€™tBelong = 593. Total nStudentBelong = 1,332; total nStudentDonâ€™tBelong = 230. See Supplemental Method for more details. Again because this overall treemap combines data from multiple academic years, some students contributed data more than once. Most students contributed to only one wave of data collection (1,484, 89.2%), some students contributed to two waves (153, 9.2%), and relatively few students contributed to three waves (27, 1.6%). Treemap was generated using the ggplot2 and treemapify packages. Colors were produced using the inferno palette of the viridis package.
